## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature relationship, a fundamental constitutive law in materials science. Temperature typically causes thermal softening (reducing elastic modulus and flow stress), while strain governs elastic and plastic deformation behavior.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elastic with T-dependent modulus)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (elastic modulus linearly dependent on temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic deformation power-law relationship)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal dependence)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear elastic with saturation)
- Hollomon with Arrhenius: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic T-dependence of modulus)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo type)
- Combined power-exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Bilinear with thermal: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * max(epsilon - c2, 0)) * exp(c3 * T) (elastic-plastic bilinear with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Stress proportional to strain multiplied by a decreasing function of temperature: epsilon * f(T) where f is decreasing
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type exponential approach: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c0/T) or exp(-c0*T) multiplying mechanical response terms
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress expression independent of strain, representing initial yield
- Power-law creep coupling → Product form epsilon**c1 * T**c2 reflecting coupled strain-rate and temperature sensitivity
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Smooth transition functions like tanh(c0*epsilon) bridging linear and saturated regimes
- Modulus degradation with temperature → Multiplicative factor (1 - (T/c0)**c1) representing approach to melting
- Strain-temperature cross terms → Products epsilon*T indicating that hardening rate depends on temperature
